  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_eec97823-7aa7-42d3-8e3e-1a2bd65f813d'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

  <span id="freeText7199838451289737489" style="display:none">Living in peaceful Shady Vale, Shea Ohmsford knew little of the troubles that plagued the rest of the world. Then the giant, forbidding Allanon revealed that the supposedly dead Warlock Lord was plotting to destroy the world. The sole weapon against this Power of Darkness was the Sword of Shannara, which could only be used by a true heir of Shannara--Shea being the last of the bloodline, upon whom all hope rested. Soon a Skull Bearer, dread minion of Evil, flew into the Vale, seeking to destroy Shea. To save the Vale, Shea fled, drawing the Skull Bearer after him....</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer105819358" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8923440946189005065"><a href='http://s153.photobucket.com/albums/s207/sullypython/Goodreads/?action=view&current=incomingbaby-1.jpg' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380335703i/694485.jpg' alt='Photobucket' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/><b>Man</b> did that ever <b>SUCK</b>. And not your garden-variety, <b>ham-fisted hackiness</b> kind of suck. No, this was <b>dumbfounded</b>, frustrated <b>bitterness</b> swelling into <b>white heat</b> for which the only salve is the venting of my smoking, <b>bile-filled</b> vitriol in the form of this <s>juvenile tantrum</s> scathing rebuke of Brooks’ abominable, <b>turd-like abortion</b> of appalling plot-stealing gall.…Therefore listen to <b>Baby Rage</b> above and take cover…*inhales deeply and launches*…<br/>.<br/>.<br/>.<br/><a href='http://s153.photobucket.com/albums/s207/sullypython/Fail/?action=view&current=explosion-fail-a-big-fat-finger-theone-epic-fail-1290706547-1-1-1.jpg' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380335703i/694486.jpg' alt='Photobucket' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/><b><u>PLOT SUMMARY</u>:</b><br/><br/>A shitty, lifeless point for po</span>
  <span id="freeText8923440946189005065" style="display:none"><a href="http://s153.photobucket.com/albums/s207/sullypython/Goodreads/?action=view&amp;current=incomingbaby-1.jpg" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380335703i/694485.jpg" alt="Photobucket" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><b>Man</b> did that ever <b>SUCK</b>. And not your garden-variety, <b>ham-fisted hackiness</b> kind of suck. No, this was <b>dumbfounded</b>, frustrated <b>bitterness</b> swelling into <b>white heat</b> for which the only salve is the venting of my smoking, <b>bile-filled</b> vitriol in the form of this <s>juvenile tantrum</s> scathing rebuke of Brooks’ abominable, <b>turd-like abortion</b> of appalling plot-stealing gall.…Therefore listen to <b>Baby Rage</b> above and take cover…*inhales deeply and launches*…<br>.<br>.<br>.<br><a href="http://s153.photobucket.com/albums/s207/sullypython/Fail/?action=view&amp;current=explosion-fail-a-big-fat-finger-theone-epic-fail-1290706547-1-1-1.jpg" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380335703i/694486.jpg" alt="Photobucket" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><b><u>PLOT SUMMARY</u>:</b><br><br>A shitty, lifeless point for point rip off of Lord of the Rings. <br><br>Seriously…that’s it.<br><br><b><u>THOUGHTS</u>:</b><br><br>Where do I begin. Well, I may have mentioned this already but it bears repeating <b>ad nauseam</b>…This book sucked. It really sucked. It sucked wookie balls, infected corpses and randy polar bears. It sucked so bad it could pull bricks through a garden hose. <br><br>This novel, and I use the term loosely and with much reservation, is a 767 page Memorex recording of Tolkien’s Lord of the Rings, except:<br><br><b>**</b> instead of a ring the quest item is a sword; <br><br><b>**</b> instead of Gandalf, Sauron, Aragorn, Boromir, Legolas, Gimli, Nazgul and Gollum, you get the Allanon, The Warlock Lord, Menion, Balinor, Durin, Hendel, Skull Bearers, Orl Fane; and <br><br><b>**</b> instead of lush, poetic prose, rich with allusions to a detailed, magnificent history and a wider world that draws you in and makes you long to look under every stone and behind every tree for some new thread of Tolkien’s magical tapestry…..you get a clunky, ill-formed world depicted by clumsy, tinny prose that fails utterly to imbue any sense of tension and emotion into the narrative….well other than outrage.<br><br>Even the back stories of these Tolkien analogs and the central plot points are lifted almost verbatim from LOTR. For example:<br><br>-- Orl Fane is a gnome, driven insane by his lustful desire for the Sword of Shannara. Hmm? Who could that be? *coughing/retching sound* <b>Galling</b>…<b>Galling</b><br><br>-- The Skull bearers are former humans who sacrificed their humanity to become the Warlord Kings most trusted servants and strike fear into the hearts of all who see them. There is even a part where one of them almost kills <s>Frodo</s> Shea.<br><br>-- Allanon, the Druid, puts <s>the Hobbits</s> Shea and Flick on the quest to find the Sword of Shannara and guides them on their travels…until of course he falls <s>at Moira</s> ….only to come back even stronger. (I’m sure I’ve read something like this before). <br><br>-- You have the initial formation of the “fellowship” to seek the Sword following the council at <s>Rivendell</s> Culhaven and a grand final battle that certainly looks like it could have been a rehearsal for the “Battle of Pelennor Fields”…only shittier and without the dramatic tension and splendor of the original. <br><br>How is it that no member of the Tolkien estate has ever bum-rushed Brooks and gone Middle Earth on his ass with a pair of pliers and a blow torch. Where is Marcellus Wallace when we need him. <br><br>In case I haven’t been as glassy and transparent as possible, let me begin my wrap up by saying, I didn’t like it. I didn’t like myself while I was reading it and I feel worse as a person for having read it. I feel soiled. <br><br>Did I mention that this is <b>767 pages</b> long? <br><br>767 pages of lifted/borrowed/stolen, clumsily altered and uninspiringly executed plot with thin, lifeless characterizations that pale like Casper in the shadow of their superior source material. There is nothing about this that I can recommend to someone, except maybe to infuse a greater appreciation for the genius that was Tolkien’s masterpiece. <br><br>1.0stars. Shame on you, Mr. Brooks. <br></span>
  <a data-text-id="8923440946189005065" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Susanne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Susanne" href="/user/show/1382568-susanne">Susanne</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

           <span class="uitext reviewText">no one... maybe Tolkien fans who DON'T mind a re-telling</span></div>

    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Susanne by: </span>
      amazon. buggers.
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1382568-susanne?shelf=couldn-t-finish">couldn-t-finish</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer30433158" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7892912826751749696">If <i>The Sword of Shannara</i> was a film, it would go like this:<br/><br/>Mirkwood Productions proudly presents:<br/><br/>THE FELLOWSHIP OF THE SWORD<br/><br/><br/>Directed by Meriadoc Brandybuck. Director of Photography: Celeborn. Costume Design: Arwen Evenstar. Visual Effects: Saruman the White. Sound Design: Noldor Unlimited. Starring Frodo Baggins, Samwise Gamgee, Gandalf the Grey, Sauron the Necromancer, Aragorn Arathornsson, Gimli van Gloin, and many more!<br/><br/>Synapsis<br/><br/>The Ohmsford brothers Shea (BAGGINS) and Flick (GAMGEE) live a pea</span>
  <span id="freeText7892912826751749696" style="display:none">If <i>The Sword of Shannara</i> was a film, it would go like this:<br /><br />Mirkwood Productions proudly presents:<br /><br />THE FELLOWSHIP OF THE SWORD<br /><br /><br />Directed by Meriadoc Brandybuck. Director of Photography: Celeborn. Costume Design: Arwen Evenstar. Visual Effects: Saruman the White. Sound Design: Noldor Unlimited. Starring Frodo Baggins, Samwise Gamgee, Gandalf the Grey, Sauron the Necromancer, Aragorn Arathornsson, Gimli van Gloin, and many more!<br /><br />Synapsis<br /><br />The Ohmsford brothers Shea (BAGGINS) and Flick (GAMGEE) live a peaceful and simple life in the Vale (SHIRE), helping their father (HAMFAST GAMGEE) run the family inn, when one day a mysterious stranger arrives in the Vale. His name is Allanon (GANDALF THE WHITE) and he has a dark and disturbing tale to tell: The Warlock Lord (an exceptional performance by the DARK LORD) has risen again. He knows that the ancient Sword of Shannara, currently being protected by the Druids in Paranor (GONDOR), is the only weapon that can permantly destroy him if wielded by a descendant of the House of Shannara. Allanon reveals to Shea that he is, in fact, part elf and carries the bloodline of Shannara. His life is in danger and he must flee the Vale at once. Allanon tells him to meet him the dwarf city of Culhaven (RIVENDELL) as soon as possible and disappears.<br /><br /><br />Hesitant to believe Allanon's tale at first, the brothers decide to wait and see if part of the stranger's story is true – that the servants of the Warlock Lord are looking for Shea. They bear a Skull Mark ™ . One night, Shea and Flick witness one of the Skull Bearers (NAZGUL) in the village and flee instantly. They must get to Culhaven somehow and decide to seek the help of their friend Menion Leah (HALDIR). Their journey takes them through the Black Oaks forest and past the Misty Marsh where they are attacked by and narrowly escape a Mist Wraith (our very own WATCHER IN THE WATER has come out of retirement to appear in this film) before they finally arrive safe and sound in Culhaven, where they meet Balinor Buckhannah (ARAGORN) and Hendel the dwarf (VAN GLOIN). A council of the Races is held under the direction of Allanon, and it is decided that a small party (FELLOWSHIP ™) must journey north and rescue the Sword of Shannara from the army of Goblins that has captured it in a raid of Paranor. etc, ad naus.<br /><br />I threw this first against the wall and then away. There's only so much derivation a woman can take...<br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7892912826751749696" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_304028656" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/304028656" />
    <a title="Nikko" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8073670-nikko"><img alt="Nikko" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1331029197p2/8073670.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/304028656?book_show_action=true">Mar 31, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nikko" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nikko" href="/user/show/8073670-nikko">Nikko</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780345274441" href="/book/show/891780.The_Sword_Of_Shannara">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer304028656" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer174027414459896041">Alright. Before anyone goes into a tirade of why I gave this book a five-star rating, read on.<br/><br/>I was never the novel-reader type. I was never much of a novelist, either. I live in a Third World country, so when I was young, we kids amuse ourselves by learning to climb trees, playing hide-and-seek and all sorts of outdoorsy games.<br/><br/>Until I met Terry Brooks through The Sword of Shannara.<br/><br/>A neighbor of ours was moving out, and with the bulk of books and other stuff they have, they decided to sell most </span>
  <span id="freeText174027414459896041" style="display:none">Alright. Before anyone goes into a tirade of why I gave this book a five-star rating, read on.<br /><br />I was never the novel-reader type. I was never much of a novelist, either. I live in a Third World country, so when I was young, we kids amuse ourselves by learning to climb trees, playing hide-and-seek and all sorts of outdoorsy games.<br /><br />Until I met Terry Brooks through The Sword of Shannara.<br /><br />A neighbor of ours was moving out, and with the bulk of books and other stuff they have, they decided to sell most of them. Ms. Susan saw me browsing through the books they were selling one afternoon, and when I was about to leave without buying anything (I had no money, since my parents never really gave me money to spend on anything until I was in High School), she beckoned me to come closer and gave me a seemingly old, yellowed-page-kind of book with the cover ripped off and no more first few pages. For an eleven year-old kid, it was kind of cradling a treasure (add that to my over-active imagination, hahaha).<br /><br />That's when I started reading. In earnest.<br /><br />The Sword of Shannara engrossed me. In bibliophyllic terms, I was heavily intoxicated, hahaha Sure, it had a very similar plotline with that of the Lord of the Rings by Tolkien (which I found out years later when I was in college already), but as you go further into the story, you would see where Brooks' originality lies. Besides, J.R.R. Tolkien is Terry Brook's mentor. It would be highly improbable if Tolkien's Middle Earth wouldn't rub off on any of his students. :D<br /><br />When I started working, I made it a point to collect all of Terry Brooks' works, from the Sword of Shannara trilogy (I bought a brand new hard cover version of The Sword of Shannara) to the Genesis of Shannara books. I would often end up comparing how beautiful was the first book, the Sword of Shannara, is compared to the rest of the following materials.<br /><br />Where others see repetition, I see consistency. Where others see a rip-off copycat work, I see one of the many variations in the seeds of literature that Tolkien sowed into the world of reading and writing.<br /><br />Terry Brooks' The Sword of Shannara will always hold a special place in my heart, as it awakened me to the world of fantasy, fiction, and magic. :)</span>
  <a data-text-id="174027414459896041" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1452736760" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1452736760" />
    <a title="Jesse (JesseTheReader)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8114361-jesse-jessethereader"><img alt="Jesse (JesseTheReader)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1550626778p2/8114361.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1452736760?book_show_action=true">Nov 26, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

<div id="review_1526593621" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1526593621" />
    <a title="Sean Barrs " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27788046-sean-barrs"><img alt="Sean Barrs " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605281953p2/27788046.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1526593621?book_show_action=true">Jan 26, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sean Barrs " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sean Barrs " href="/user/show/27788046-sean-barrs">Sean Barrs </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781841495484" href="/book/show/891775.The_Sword_of_Shannara">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27788046-sean-barrs?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27788046-sean-barrs?shelf=love-and-romance">love-and-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27788046-sean-barrs?shelf=4-star-reads">4-star-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1526593621" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5880964805886295750">Now this is what I like to see in a fantasy novel. This has everything that makes the genre so appealing to me; it’s got a diverse set of races and cultural systems; it’s got both great darkness and profound good. But, most importantly, it’s got history. When I read books like this I want to feel like the fantasy universe has existed a thousand years prior and will exist a thousand years after. With Shannara it feels like I’ve stepped into the middle of a vast, complex and beautiful world that h</span>
  <span id="freeText5880964805886295750" style="display:none">Now this is what I like to see in a fantasy novel. This has everything that makes the genre so appealing to me; it’s got a diverse set of races and cultural systems; it’s got both great darkness and profound good. But, most importantly, it’s got history. When I read books like this I want to feel like the fantasy universe has existed a thousand years prior and will exist a thousand years after. With Shannara it feels like I’ve stepped into the middle of a vast, complex and beautiful world that has always been, and always will be. <br><br><b> The Epic Quest </b><br><br> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1454850343i/18021825._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The wonderful adventure begins with two young men, a wise and powerful historian and destiny, the mightiest force of all. One of the men is a decedent to the long dead elven King Shannara. His name is Shae and he is destined to wield his ancestor’s sword, the only weapon capable of destroying the mighty Warlock Lord, and bringing an end to the tension that is about to cause an all-out war. Does this sound familiar? I will address the Tolkien parallels later on in my review. So bear with me. Shae has no experience in adventure; he has spent most of his life in his father’s inn, so he has a mighty task ahead of him. One in which he is, naturally, reluctant to undertake. You see, his life was fairly ordinary till the historian, Allanon, appeared and informed him of his quest. <br><br>Shae and his brother Flick turn to their friend for help. Well, I say friend, I mean to say Shae’s friend. Flick hates Menion Leah; he thinks he is a reckless waste of space. This makes for a rather awkward and funny group dynamic, one that sees a reluctant hero in the middle of his two greatest friends that don’t stop bickering. The trio depart, run into a heap of trouble, and get unbelievably lost. The situation is amusing and desperate. Shae does find his courage though, as he learns to wield the ancient elf stones that the historian gave him. They run into more danger, and later more allies, as the historian urges Shae ever closer to his all too important destiny. <br><br><b> A party of desperation </b><br><br>It quickly becomes clear that this is no simple adventure story. I was really quite glad of this because it made the last parts of it really intense. The group is forced to split up, and rouse the allied forced to stand against the huge incoming invasion. It’s all tied up with Shae’s destiny. Evil is striking first with the purpose of preventing him from claiming the only weapon capable of severing the darkness. It’s one big race of survival with legions of foes marching on the lands of the heroes. The sword is the only hope of victory. <br><br><i>“Herein lies the heart and soul of the nations.<br>Their right to be free men,<br>Their desire to live in peace,<br>Their courage to seek out truth,<br>Herein lies the Sword of Shannara.”</i><br><br> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1454850343i/18021826.jpg" width="400" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>However, there’s more to it than that. Brook’s forces of evil are not just some twisted things form the darkness. They are races of goblins and trolls, which are like the heroes. They have been manipulated into serving a greater power. They are not without redemption; they do not have black hearts; they have simply had their free will stole from them, and then unleashed in a brutal war. This, for me, made the entire conflict quite interesting; it meant that there could be both great evil and good on both sides. This can be seen with the great betrayal and the rock trolls that show reactance when they find Shae. It felt like a real war, but in a fantastical setting. <br><br><b> Is it too Tolkienesque? </b><br><br>Is such a thing possible? Brooks has borrowed heavily from Tolkien, and I mean heavily. More so than any other author I’ve read. Robert Jordan did this too, but with Brooks the entire structure of the novel is like a condensed version of the Lord of the Rings Trilogy. Not only are there similar characters, uncannily so, but there is also an almost exact replica of the siege of Minas Tirith. However, the book is still worth a read. Certainly, the crossovers are a little annoying in parts but, as a huge fan of the genre, I cannot simply overlook what Terry Brooks does well. This is his first novel, and whist it resembles Tolkien’s world, I know that his later books don’t entirely. <br><br>I think this book should be approached with a very open mind. It’s a simple stepping stone that Brooks has used to go on and explore his own world in greater depth in later books. It’s almost like he has used Tolkien as a crutch to get himself started with his own writing. I can’t condemn the book for this reason alone. Moreover, I like his writing style and his own influence can be seen in later books of fantasy, and even some video games such as The Elder Scrolls franchise and World of Warcraft. There are original aspects in here, though they are few in number.<br><br>Tolkien’s story was also that excellent that when a few early fantasy writers regurgitated it, it wasn’t completely terrible. They could get away with it because they were the first to do it. I have no major problems seeing the repetition here; this is a great fantasy adventure. I urge other readers to try it for themselves before they shun the author because of his copycat label because, in this case, it’s not necessarily a bad thing. I, for one, will be reading the rest of the trilogy. However, I am hoping for improvements in the writing. I’m willing to enjoy this book in good humour, as it’s the author’s first book, but if the similarity is constant I may not persist in reading another trilogy. <br><br><u>The Original Shannara Trilogy </u><br>1. The Sword of Shannara- <b> Four worthy stars </b></span>
  <a data-text-id="5880964805886295750" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_51019101" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/51019101" />
    <a title="Kat  Hooper" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2177891-kat-hooper"><img alt="Kat  Hooper" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1533675060p2/2177891.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/51019101?book_show_action=true">Mar 31, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kat  Hooper" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kat  Hooper" href="/user/show/2177891-kat-hooper">Kat  Hooper</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer51019101" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7741002573019132559">ORIGINALLY POSTED AT <a href='http://www.fantasyliterature.com' rel='nofollow noopener'>Fantasy Literature</a>.<br/><br/>The Sword of Shannara was a very popular book back in the 70s right after the huge success of The Lord of the Rings when everyone wanted to read more fantasy. I wasn't old enough to read it back then, so I came to it much later. I read part of the first book and, knowing how popular it had been, and feeling like it was a classic, I was prepared to enjoy it. About half way through I gave it to my ten year old son.<br/><br/>The weird thing is, it's so like The Lord of</span>
  <span id="freeText7741002573019132559" style="display:none">ORIGINALLY POSTED AT <a href="http://www.fantasyliterature.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Fantasy Literature</a>.<br /><br />The Sword of Shannara was a very popular book back in the 70s right after the huge success of The Lord of the Rings when everyone wanted to read more fantasy. I wasn't old enough to read it back then, so I came to it much later. I read part of the first book and, knowing how popular it had been, and feeling like it was a classic, I was prepared to enjoy it. About half way through I gave it to my ten year old son.<br /><br />The weird thing is, it's so like The Lord of the Rings, at the same time that it's not. I don't mind a few common fantasy elements (especially in works written before they were cliché), but Brooks' plot and characters come almost straight out of Tolkien. This may have been acceptable if the writing had come straight out of Tolkien, too, but Brooks' style is clunky, wordy, and awkward. Adjectives and adverbs are used without restraint. I mean there are constant repetitive superfluous unnecessary redundant profligate excessive numbers of adjectives. And did I mention the weirdly-placed adverbs which are used unsparingly, unrestrainedly, extravagantly, and immoderately? And annoyingly? . . . When I couldn't care less whether Shea and Flick (they're the hobbits-- I mean the heroes) live or die, then the characterization is weak. Actually, I was kind of hoping that they would die. If they died, the book would have to end, right?<br /><br />Conclusion: These are fine for kids (at least this one is, I can't say if all of the later Shannara books are -- probably not). But, do you really want to teach them to write like that? If not, give them C.S. Lewis, J.K. Rowling, Susan Cooper, and Lloyd Alexander. To be fair: This series is wildly popular. Perhaps the writing gets better (it has been 30 years, after all). I have heard that only the first book is too much like Tolkien. But I'll never know for sure because I can't make it through the first one. <br /><br />Read more <a href="http://www.fantasyliterature.com/brooksterry.html" rel="nofollow noopener"> Terry Brooks reviews at <i>Fantasy Literature </i></a></span>
  <a data-text-id="7741002573019132559" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_6366489" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Lorena" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/251417-lorena"><img alt="Lorena" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1489184320p2/251417.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/6366489?book_show_action=true">Sep 17, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lorena" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lorena" href="/user/show/251417-lorena">Lorena</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/251417-lorena?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer6366489" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7641388036945918186">A friend who was also into fantasy insisted I read this series, and I got as far as the first three books before I stopped believing him when he told me they were magical and wonderful and would get better and better. As far as I can tell, they all have the exact same plot. Mysterious Wizard shows up at home of person. Tells person he is Chosen for an Important Quest. What follows is chapter after chapter of "I don't WANNA go on a Quest!" "You MUST go on a Quest!" Seriously, I know the reluctant</span>
  <span id="freeText7641388036945918186" style="display:none">A friend who was also into fantasy insisted I read this series, and I got as far as the first three books before I stopped believing him when he told me they were magical and wonderful and would get better and better. As far as I can tell, they all have the exact same plot. Mysterious Wizard shows up at home of person. Tells person he is Chosen for an Important Quest. What follows is chapter after chapter of "I don't WANNA go on a Quest!" "You MUST go on a Quest!" Seriously, I know the reluctant hero who doesn't want to/feel worthy of/is afraid of his Quest is a staple of fantasy literature, but this series takes it to a whole new level - the perpetually petulant hero. Nothing but whine, whine, whine through the whole damn book. And then the book ends, with our hero crabby but triumphant and returning home, and the Mysterious Wizard apparently dead or missing. Only to turn up again at the beginning of the next book to browbeat the next whiny member of the Chosen Family to go on HIS Quest. Lather, rinse, repeat. <br /><br />Oh, and the writing sucks, too. </span>
  <a data-text-id="7641388036945918186" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_162647271" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/162647271" />
    <a title="mark monday" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/131922-mark-monday"><img alt="mark monday" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1572672245p2/131922.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/162647271?book_show_action=true">Apr 21, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="mark monday" class="user" itemprop="url" name="mark monday" href="/user/show/131922-mark-monday">mark monday</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/131922-mark-monday?shelf=fantasy-60s-70s-80s">fantasy-60s-70s-80s</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer162647271" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13144460628730720095">this is perhaps my first experience with a Bad Book. young nerds like myself shouldn't have to scorn fantasy literature, but this wet piece of crapola put me off of fantasy for years. something this derivative should never have seen the light of day. i don't care if folks needed a tolkien fix, there were other, better literary drugs out there they could have turned to. Brooks spends a very long time blowing tolkien style, but it is an extremely un-relaxing bj and i found myself getting agitated </span>
  <span id="freeText13144460628730720095" style="display:none">this is perhaps my first experience with a Bad Book. young nerds like myself shouldn't have to scorn fantasy literature, but this wet piece of crapola put me off of fantasy for years. something this derivative should never have seen the light of day. i don't care if folks needed a tolkien fix, there were other, better literary drugs out there they could have turned to. Brooks spends a very long time blowing tolkien style, but it is an extremely un-relaxing bj and i found myself getting agitated every other page. watch those teeth, Terry, you're supposed to be a professional. those aren't sighs of relaxation, those are sighs of irritation and disgust. and isn't plagiarism against the law? this is High Crap of the first order.</span>

<div id="review_1711872247" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1711872247" />
    <a title="Dannii Elle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/44487975-dannii-elle"><img alt="Dannii Elle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1508499419p2/44487975.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1711872247?book_show_action=true">Jul 28, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dannii Elle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dannii Elle" href="/user/show/44487975-dannii-elle">Dannii Elle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781841495484" href="/book/show/891775.The_Sword_of_Shannara">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44487975-dannii-elle?shelf=fantastic-fabrications">fantastic-fabrications</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1711872247" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8762722666509625917">Wow - that is pretty much all I could say for hours after finishing this absolutely epic first installment in the Shannara series.<br/><br/>This book gave me everything I want in my fantasies - a vast landscape, colossal amounts of world-building, varied characters, mythical and mystical creatures, a definite good/bad binary, a quest to save the world, great character development, legions of backstory, action, adventure and intrigue, and ending on a battle scent to end all battle scenes.<br/><br/>The best fantasies</span>
  <span id="freeText8762722666509625917" style="display:none">Wow - that is pretty much all I could say for hours after finishing this absolutely epic first installment in the Shannara series.<br /><br />This book gave me everything I want in my fantasies - a vast landscape, colossal amounts of world-building, varied characters, mythical and mystical creatures, a definite good/bad binary, a quest to save the world, great character development, legions of backstory, action, adventure and intrigue, and ending on a battle scent to end all battle scenes.<br /><br />The best fantasies are always hefty tomes and this one was no exception! This enabled the story to provide everything from the list above (and then some!), whilst still not overshadowing the epic plot and the journey across this fantastical landscape to conclude the adventures detailed.<br /><br />I did, however, have some minor gripes with this novel. Firstly, the omittance of all but one female character made this immediately drop a star rating! The one solitary female in the entirety of the 664 pages felt like she was only included to play the damsel in distress and allow for a heroic rescue by one of the main male characters. Bleurgh!<br /><br />Also, there seemed to be many instances where the 'baddies' were thwarted at the last second without giving a full explanation as to how or why. There were plenty of fully explained and chapter-long battle scenes but some early incidents see the main characters escape without themselves even realizing how they did so. Some moments didn't feel real, for this reason, and would have really benefitted from some padding out.<br /><br />In all, I can forgive this its minor sins as there was SO much to love about this fantastical journey, and I can't wait to join back in with the escapades of this already beloved cast in the next installment.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8762722666509625917" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_452125422" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/452125422" />
    <a title="Evgeny" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9340136-evgeny"><img alt="Evgeny" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1544797852p2/9340136.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/452125422?book_show_action=true">Nov 09, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Evgeny" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Evgeny" href="/user/show/9340136-evgeny">Evgeny</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9340136-evgeny?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer452125422" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9138567938083988312">A mysterious stranger came into a peaceful village of Shady Vale. From him one of the village boys learned about being the last hope of vanquishing an ancient evil with the legendary Sword of Shannara. I am not going to go deep inside the plot as it was used numerous times after this book; it fact the book can be partially blamed for almost all of fantasy with a poor farm boy/girl destined to be the last humanity savior. The rest of the blame goes to The Lord of the Rings.<br/><br/>The general consensus a</span>
  <span id="freeText9138567938083988312" style="display:none">A mysterious stranger came into a peaceful village of Shady Vale. From him one of the village boys learned about being the last hope of vanquishing an ancient evil with the legendary Sword of Shannara. I am not going to go deep inside the plot as it was used numerous times after this book; it fact the book can be partially blamed for almost all of fantasy with a poor farm boy/girl destined to be the last humanity savior. The rest of the blame goes to The Lord of the Rings.<br /><br />The general consensus about the book is that it is a carbon copy of Tolkien's writings. While I agree that the overall structure of the book is closely resembles that of the father of modern fantasy, the characters and the plot were different enough to be interesting. Regarding the characters I will be the first one to admit Allanon is a copy of Gandalf, but even he feels more human and fleshed out with the rest of the characters showing more grey sides of them, not just typical black and white. <br /><br />Another feature which impressed me about the book: it gives a lot of good description of places, nature, people, etc. These descriptions are always to the point, never go into rambling mode and not boring. I can name some well-known writers who can spend a couple of pages describing a woman's dress, or even entire chapters dedicating to dishes of a fest; this book does not do it. This is something I really miss in modern writings - and I am not talking about just fantasy genre. <br /><br />To my surprise the book wrapped up all of its plot lines in the end completely despite being called first book in a trilogy. So there you have it: an epic fantasy in fewer than 600 pages. I really forgot the last time I read anything epic and relatively short. <br /><br />All in all this is a well written novel different enough from Tolkien to warrant 4 stars. </span>
  <a data-text-id="9138567938083988312" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText7052282211722314998" style="display:none">I loved this when I was thirteen. <br /><br />I loved it when I was sixteen. And probably at least once in between there. <br /><br />When I was thirty-six I picked it up, made it about a chapter and a half in, and threw it against the wall. <br /><br />Literally. <br /><br />It left a dent. <br /><br /><i>(Edited for the trolls among you: A- this is a touch of hyperbole. Look it up. <br /><br />and<br /><br />B- It's a 700+ page book, and I was incensed. It's not entirely inconceivable that this thing <b>would</b> dent the drywall.<br /><br />Just saying. Back to the original review... )</i><br /><br />This book was written before fan-fic was quite so mainstream. There were no fic websites out there then – there were no websites then. There was still fan-fic, printed in little fanzines and passed around among friends and such. And then there was this sort of thing, perpetrated on a public that had been introduced to wonder in the form of elves and wizards and quests, and who wanted more of it. Terry Brooks saw a market, and he acted to take advantage of it. I've read here and there that bad as this one is, the rest of the series improves – it couldn't get much worse, I have to say. But this: this is shameful.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7052282211722314998" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

      </span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26681101-markus?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26681101-markus?shelf=2014">2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26681101-markus?shelf=post-apocalyptic">post-apocalyptic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26681101-markus?shelf=shannara">shannara</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer793271779" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14369603302564205451">The Sword of Shannara is basically The Lord of the Rings version 2.0. It is also one of the best fantasy novels I have ever read.<br/><br/>The book was first recommended to me by my father and uncle at a family gathering last year (I should clarify that 'recommended' here means 'briefly mentioned during a short discussion about good literature'). I had not read a fantasy novel for quite a while and was in search of something to read, so I found the book in one of my parents' bookshelves and brought it wit</span>
  <span id="freeText14369603302564205451" style="display:none">The Sword of Shannara is basically The Lord of the Rings version 2.0. It is also one of the best fantasy novels I have ever read.<br /><br />The book was first recommended to me by my father and uncle at a family gathering last year (I should clarify that 'recommended' here means 'briefly mentioned during a short discussion about good literature'). I had not read a fantasy novel for quite a while and was in search of something to read, so I found the book in one of my parents' bookshelves and brought it with me when I went to India this winter. I was enthralled.<br /><br />The book is a tale of Shea Ohmsford, a rather normal boy living in a peaceful valley far away from any sort of action or adventure. That is, until the mysterious druid Allanon appears and tells Shea that he is the last heir to the legacy of the mythic House of Shannara; once the rulers of the elven people and now long gone.<br /><br />When it is then revealed that the dreaded Warlock Lord has returned from supposed death to destroy the world, Shea must embark upon a journey to find the long-lost Sword of Shannara, for he is the only one left who can wield it to keep the darkness at bay.<br /><br />Based on my own opinion and all the reviews I have read, you either love or hate this book. As for myself, I would recommend it to everyone, in particular those who have read authors like Tolkien and want to experience more of the same, or those looking for an introduction to the genre of fantasy. For me it was a great way to return to it, and a great introduction to a wonderful series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14369603302564205451" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1065239" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18181454611136203422">If you are comparing the literary value of science fiction/fantasy books, I think it is best to use food as an example. Terry Brooks can be viewed as a really good bacon cheeseburger, it is fun to eat, makes you feel full, however it is often sloppily put together in a hurried fashion, without much effort and does not give your body true fulfillment. <br/><br/>While Tolkien on the other hand, or C.S. Lewis, are like well planned home cooked meals, with each food group represented and placed on a finely se</span>
  <span id="freeText18181454611136203422" style="display:none">If you are comparing the literary value of science fiction/fantasy books, I think it is best to use food as an example. Terry Brooks can be viewed as a really good bacon cheeseburger, it is fun to eat, makes you feel full, however it is often sloppily put together in a hurried fashion, without much effort and does not give your body true fulfillment. <br /><br />While Tolkien on the other hand, or C.S. Lewis, are like well planned home cooked meals, with each food group represented and placed on a finely set dining table. Both are food, and both are great in their own respects. Just very different in execution and planning. I do like Brook's vision of the fantasy races and world formed by the aftereffects of a devastating nuclear war sometime in the near future. </span>
  <a data-text-id="18181454611136203422" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8287314426661127537">When I was but an impressionable teen, my crush gave me this book for my birthday. He had teeth like little baby pearls and could quote from The Princess Bride, so I was pretty far gone on him. This book was so bad that it effectively cured me of that crush. Despite being a plot-point-for-plot-point, character-for-character rip-off of the Lord of the Rings, it's pretty boring. In fact, the only surprise in this novel is that despite such blatant plagiarism, none of the beauty of Tolkein's descri</span>
  <span id="freeText8287314426661127537" style="display:none">When I was but an impressionable teen, my crush gave me this book for my birthday. He had teeth like little baby pearls and could quote from The Princess Bride, so I was pretty far gone on him. This book was so bad that it effectively cured me of that crush. Despite being a plot-point-for-plot-point, character-for-character rip-off of the Lord of the Rings, it's pretty boring. In fact, the only surprise in this novel is that despite such blatant plagiarism, none of the beauty of Tolkein's descriptions or rich history of his peoples translates over. I don't know how Brooks managed to strip Tolkein's tales of everything wonderful and beautiful, but he did it somehow.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8287314426661127537" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_7822205" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/7822205" />
    <a title="Hollyhocks" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/59789-hollyhocks"><img alt="Hollyhocks" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1193529874p2/59789.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/7822205?book_show_action=true">Oct 16, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hollyhocks" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hollyhocks" href="/user/show/59789-hollyhocks">Hollyhocks</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">epic adventurers</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer7822205" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13769806426302992585">So, I've read reviews that say this is just Terry Brooks' Lord of the Rings. I do see that, but at the same time, I think he made it his own in a lot of ways. I mean, aren't all fantasy adventures just someone's take on Lord of the Rings ... anyway, other than the fact that it's 700-some pages and I thought I would never finish it .. I liked it. I wasn't happy that 2 of the characters I liked died, but, it was a battle-adventure, can't live happily-ever-after for everyone. There were some lullin</span>
  <span id="freeText13769806426302992585" style="display:none">So, I've read reviews that say this is just Terry Brooks' Lord of the Rings. I do see that, but at the same time, I think he made it his own in a lot of ways. I mean, aren't all fantasy adventures just someone's take on Lord of the Rings ... anyway, other than the fact that it's 700-some pages and I thought I would never finish it .. I liked it. I wasn't happy that 2 of the characters I liked died, but, it was a battle-adventure, can't live happily-ever-after for everyone. There were some lulling and overly-descriptive areas but mainly it was a page-turner, especially when just as one story-line was getting to a climax, he'd change to a different side of the story .. that was great to keep me reading. I've read Eragon and can see where that author was heavily influenced by this book, at least it seems to me he was. All this book was missing was a dragon .. haha .. <br />Anyway, it's worth a read. I really enjoyed it!</span>
  <a data-text-id="13769806426302992585" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2535336328" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2535336328" />
    <a title="Malum" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/68337677-malum"><img alt="Malum" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1518964187p2/68337677.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2535336328?book_show_action=true">Sep 20, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Malum" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Malum" href="/user/show/68337677-malum">Malum</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68337677-malum?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2535336328" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15979713187471052971">“Immature poets imitate; mature poets steal"<br/>-T.S. Eliot<br/><br/>Terry Brooks-by his own admission-was a failed author until someone put a copy of J.R.R. Tolkien's <i>The Lord of the Rings</i> into his hands. Suddenly, he became a very successful published author of fantasy novels. Was this some kind of magic? Perhaps divine inspiration? Nope. It was pure, unadulterated theft. <br/><br/>Now, there are two kinds of people that seem to be writing reviews for this book. The first kind of person hates it because it really is </span>
  <span id="freeText15979713187471052971" style="display:none">“Immature poets imitate; mature poets steal"<br />-T.S. Eliot<br /><br />Terry Brooks-by his own admission-was a failed author until someone put a copy of J.R.R. Tolkien's <i>The Lord of the Rings</i> into his hands. Suddenly, he became a very successful published author of fantasy novels. Was this some kind of magic? Perhaps divine inspiration? Nope. It was pure, unadulterated theft. <br /><br />Now, there are two kinds of people that seem to be writing reviews for this book. The first kind of person hates it because it really is just Tolkien's masterpiece with the names changed. I don't know who published this or why Brook's wasn't sued into oblivion, but he doesn't even try to hide the fact that this book is largely not his own work. The same characters, the same plot points, and even some of the same exact scenes are copied from <i>The Lord of the Rings</i> and dropped into this book. <br /><br />The second kind of person rates this book pretty highly, and almost always adds a weak "Well, there are a lot of things that are different, too...". These people are either knowingly or subconsciously giving this book a pass that it doesn't deserve. Yes, there are a few things that are a little different here and there, but to make that small fact the saving grace of this book is extremely disingenuous. <br /><br />As for my own personal opinion, I can freely admit that this book is a totally unoriginal con-job and still rate it rather highly. Why? Because I like <i>The Lord of the Rings</i> and so I am predisposed to liking a book that is almost the same thing. I am not taking off stars because of some kind of self-righteous anger, and at the same time I am not giving this book a pass by writing a review meekly explaining away its shady history.<br /><br />Looked at independently of its source material, I only have a few notes:<br /><br />Things I liked:<br />It was rarely boring. Things moved at a nice pace for most of this pretty long novel. <br /><br />It wrapped up its story in one book. Yes, I know the Shannara brand has about 20 books out at the moment, but this one doesn't really end on a cliffhanger and you can put it down without feeling like you have to move on to the next. The idea that every fantasy story has to be at least a trilogy is a cancer that has been eating away at the genre for a long time now. If Tolkien's publisher had just let him print the damn thing in one big volume we wouldn't have this problem, but what can you do?<br /><br />The world's background was interesting, if not a little under developed (in book 1, at least). The world is basically our world after a nuclear holocaust wiped out most of the planet's life. Slowly, life reemerged as fantasy races and magic replaced science. Fun. <br /><br />Things I didn't like (besides the aforementioned plagiarism, of which you could write an entire book about):<br />The fellowship (sorry. Hunting party) members were all pretty bland and were practically interchangeable for most of the story. <br /><br />The big battle scenes were pretty bad. Here is an example of what the big battle scenes are like: "The enemy lined up their cavalry, but they were driven back by the pikemen. Then, a unit of swordsmen got into formation and charged the enemy line, causing them to break. From the battlements, archers fired their bows, killing half of an enemy unit". It's just "This happens. Then this happens. Then this happens. Then this happens". You feel like you are a bird watching these random masses of people moving and shuffling around without really feeling like you are in the midst of the action in any way. <br /><br />I mentioned that I liked the world background, but the fact that it wasn't really developed is a problem at times. We are basically in a fantasy world, for example, and suddenly a random robot attacks the characters. It just felt a little cheesy and out of place without delving more into the ancient (pre nuclear holocaust) history of the world. In fact, the background of the world was so quickly mentioned and forgotten that it seems like Brooks threw that in there just so he could have a random robot attack. <br /><br />So there you have it. <i>The Sword of Shannara</i> is a blatant rip off of <i>The Lord of the Rings</i> that deserves NO excuses or pardons, and yet it can still be enjoyed for what it is. Shocking, right?</span>
  <a data-text-id="15979713187471052971" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2023245776" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2023245776" />
    <a title="Jason Koivu" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1742824-jason-koivu"><img alt="Jason Koivu" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1560521450p2/1742824.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2023245776?book_show_action=true">Jun 22, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jason Koivu" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jason Koivu" href="/user/show/1742824-jason-koivu">Jason Koivu</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1742824-jason-koivu?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1742824-jason-koivu?shelf=don-t-let-me-down-dangit-you-did">don-t-let-me-down-dangit-you-did</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1742824-jason-koivu?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2023245776" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13918238587258222120">How is it Terry Brooks did not get sued by the Tolkien estate for this book? He went to law school, how could he not see the lawsuit in this?<br/><br/><i>The Sword of Shannara</i> parallels the <i>Lord of the Rings</i> series on so many points it's laughable. About a third of the way in I began to feel deja vu, like I was rereading <i>The Fellowship of the Ring</i>. There are best-bud insignificant protagonists, who are told to go on an adventure by a mysterious wizardy type guy. During the mini-starter adventure they nearly </span>
  <span id="freeText13918238587258222120" style="display:none">How is it Terry Brooks did not get sued by the Tolkien estate for this book? He went to law school, how could he not see the lawsuit in this?<br /><br /><i>The Sword of Shannara</i> parallels the <i>Lord of the Rings</i> series on so many points it's laughable. About a third of the way in I began to feel deja vu, like I was rereading <i>The Fellowship of the Ring</i>. There are best-bud insignificant protagonists, who are told to go on an adventure by a mysterious wizardy type guy. During the mini-starter adventure they nearly get done in by undeadish dudes and meet a ranger, who is an aloof royal. They meet back up in a safe haven (dwarf this time, not elf) to discuss who and how they shall proceed in their questing against the ultimate evil "dark lord". The similarities go on and on.<br /><br />But hey, enough of my yakkin'! The fact is, this is an epic work with some interesting elements, some of which do tarry from LotR territory. Imitation being the sincerest form of flattery, I feel like Brooks' heart was in the right place. And if nothing else, he was young, enthusiastic and inexperienced. For his legion of fans, it's for the best this book was not buried in legal proceedings and that its author was able to launch a long and fruitful career, for which many readers are grateful.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13918238587258222120" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1949526033" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1949526033" />
    <a title="seak" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1805180-seak"><img alt="seak" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1410456529p2/1805180.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1949526033?book_show_action=true">Apr 01, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="seak" class="user" itemprop="url" name="seak" href="/user/show/1805180-seak">seak</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1805180-seak?shelf=audio">audio</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1805180-seak?shelf=2017">2017</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1949526033" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1406356055982416902">When I finished The Lord of the Rings, all I wanted was more Lord of the Rings. And by that, what I mean is that I wanted that feeling I had while reading LotR, being lost in a world all its own and being so close to characters I considered friends. <br/><br/>That's why I think I get the appeal for The Sword of Shannara and honestly after all the reviews I've read, I expected this book to be much more close to LotR than it is. And going back to my first point, that's why I sought this book out, I was look</span>
  <span id="freeText1406356055982416902" style="display:none">When I finished The Lord of the Rings, all I wanted was more Lord of the Rings. And by that, what I mean is that I wanted that feeling I had while reading LotR, being lost in a world all its own and being so close to characters I considered friends. <br /><br />That's why I think I get the appeal for The Sword of Shannara and honestly after all the reviews I've read, I expected this book to be much more close to LotR than it is. And going back to my first point, that's why I sought this book out, I was looking for more LotR since I heard it was a carbon copy.<br /><br />Now that's not to say I couldn't go down the list of LotR characters and name a corresponding Shannara character. It's quite easy actually.<br /><br />But even then, you can tell that Brooks did go beyond the exact same story. Now, please remember beyond does not equal better, by no means. LotR remains my all-time favorite books and this book gets nowhere close, but I do acknowledge the differences were at least enough for me. Those differences also show the shortcomings with this book, since that character depth is clearly lacking.<br /><br />Yes Menion Leah is your Aragon character, but he's unknown royalty from an all but unknown kingdom. Not destined to be the returned king, he's just a straight-forward dude, loyal and brave.<br /><br />Yes, Allanon is your Gandalf, but he's also the last one of his kind and he ... disappears for no reason all the time.<br /><br />Yes, Shea is Frodo, but he's half-elf and this is more of a farmboy becomes great fantasy cliche than a Frodo who's great because of who he is. Completely different.<br /><br />Yes, the Sword of Shannara is the ring, but it's missing most of the book and doesn't ... do the same stuff. We'll leave it at that.<br /><br />I could keep going, but I'll quit there. Suffice it to say, the differences worked for me to make this its own story.<br /><br />Having known it was a carbon copy, the similar elements didn't put me off as much as it could have I'm sure. I enjoyed The Sword of Shannara as a straight-forward quest/battle book. I thought it was enjoyable and had more surprises than I thought it would despite being cliche (or originator of many cliches?). <br /><br />It completely lacks the depth of LotR, of course, (what doesn't) but it works at what it's doing and done competently. I'll read more.<br /><br />3.5 out of 5 Stars (recommended)<br /><br />Note on Narration: It's Scott Brick. Need I say more?</span>
  <a data-text-id="1406356055982416902" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1692450632" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1692450632" />
    <a title="Eric Allen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6229358-eric-allen"><img alt="Eric Allen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1560117879p2/6229358.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1692450632?book_show_action=true">Jul 08, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Eric Allen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Eric Allen" href="/user/show/6229358-eric-allen">Eric Allen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1692450632" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4848583796557579775">I grew up with the Shannara series. Along with The Wheel of Time, The Sword of Truth, and A Song of Ice and Fire, it was one of the big fantasy series that I read through numerous times and eagerly awaited more books from the author. I recently discovered the MTV (weird, but whatever) TV series The Shannara Chronicles, which was like a low budget version of Game of Thrones if it was made by drunk frat boys, starring all their jock and cheerleader friends, and John Rhys Davies, because why not. I</span>
  <span id="freeText4848583796557579775" style="display:none">I grew up with the Shannara series. Along with The Wheel of Time, The Sword of Truth, and A Song of Ice and Fire, it was one of the big fantasy series that I read through numerous times and eagerly awaited more books from the author. I recently discovered the MTV (weird, but whatever) TV series The Shannara Chronicles, which was like a low budget version of Game of Thrones if it was made by drunk frat boys, starring all their jock and cheerleader friends, and John Rhys Davies, because why not. In other words, fun-ish, but full of cheese, questionable acting, silly special effects, and a whole lot of douche. I felt the desire to go back and read a few old favorites from the books.<br /><br />This book came out something like 40 years ago, and at the time, the Fantasy Genre as we know it was relatively new. You had Tolkien, Jack Vance, a couple others, but the genre was still relatively new and fresh, without anything having become too cliche or overused yet. The adolescents from an obscure village told by a stern wizzardly fellow that they have to leave because one of them just might be the chosen one and Count Evil Von Murderkill over there will totally murderkill them if they don't, cue the Lord of the Rings Fanfare, storyline hadn't really be so overused as it is today. I'm really sad to say this, because I LOVED this book twenty-five years ago, but if Terry Brooks were to take it to a publisher in this day and age, he would likely be turned away because of how generic it is. At the time it was written, the storyline wasn't as cliche as it is today, but, the genre as a whole has done a lot of moving on from that point now.<br /><br />The book has a lot of nostalgia value for me, but in the forty years since it's publication, the Fantasy Genre has moved on to bigger and better things. Three stars is all I can give it today, even with nostaliga factored into the rating.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4848583796557579775" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
