<div id="review_10674282" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/10674282" />
    <a title="Jim" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/695116-jim"><img alt="Jim" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1340192527p2/695116.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/10674282?book_show_action=true">Dec 19, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jim" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jim" href="/user/show/695116-jim">Jim</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/695116-jim?shelf=3series">3series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/695116-jim?shelf=1paper">1paper</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/695116-jim?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/695116-jim?shelf=2fiction">2fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/695116-jim?shelf=sword-sorcery">sword-sorcery</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer10674282" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3803375595524480527"><b>
  <i>This Book</i>
</b> came out & I jumped on it. I was a real fan of the Lord of the Rings - so much so that I recited the first several pages of the Hobbit when we read it in class during the 6th grade - & this looked similar. I was ecstatic because I'd waited so long for another epic journey of that sort! <b>How could I be so lucky? Star Wars & now a new Tolkien-like saga?!!! The gods must be good!</b><br/><br/>Then I read it & almost wept in frustration. It was too similar to <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/5907.The_Hobbit' title='The Hobbit by J.R.R. Tolkien' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Hobbit</a>. Wasn't it plagiarism? This wa</span>
  <span id="freeText3803375595524480527" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>This Book</i>
</b> came out &amp; I jumped on it. I was a real fan of the Lord of the Rings - so much so that I recited the first several pages of the Hobbit when we read it in class during the 6th grade - &amp; this looked similar. I was ecstatic because I'd waited so long for another epic journey of that sort! <b>How could I be so lucky? Star Wars &amp; now a new Tolkien-like saga?!!! The gods must be good!</b><br /><br />Then I read it &amp; almost wept in frustration. It was too similar to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/5907.The_Hobbit" title="The Hobbit by J.R.R. Tolkien" rel="nofollow noopener">The Hobbit</a>. Wasn't it plagiarism? This was published by Del Rey - Lester Del Ray, the guy that brought me the Lancer editions of Conan. How could he publish something like <b>
  <i>This Book</i>
</b>?!!! I was shattered. <b>Yes, Virginia, there are BAD authors out there &amp; unscrupulous publishers!</b><br /><br />My grandfather was a newspaperman, publisher &amp; owner of one of the largest privately owned newspapers in the country. I grew up respecting the institution &amp; waited for them to smash those that would dare publish such trash. But <b>
  <i>This Book</i>
</b> made it to the prestigious New York Times best seller list! It was the first fantasy novel to do so &amp; received even more praise &amp; attention because of it. Something was horribly wrong with the world. <br /><br />It took me a decade to begin to forgive Brooks for <b>
  <i>This Book</i>
</b>. Then I read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15547.Magic_Kingdom_For_Sale_Sold__Magic_Kingdom_of_Landover___1_" title="Magic Kingdom For Sale/Sold (Magic Kingdom of Landover, #1) by Terry Brooks" rel="nofollow noopener">Magic Kingdom For Sale/Sold</a> &amp; liked it. I thought I'd give <b>
  <i>This Book</i>
</b> another shot. Maybe I was misremembering - it had been the 70's after all. (If you were really there, the memories are kind of hazy.) Unfortunately, I wasn't &amp; remembered it far too clearly, even after the mind altering substances that had passed my way. It was like a nightmare. I barely cracked <b>
  <i>This Book</i>
</b> before throwing it down again. I also found that the series had grown to a huge number of books - another betrayal. <b>How could people pay this man for his perfidy &amp; make him a success?!!!</b><br /><br />I've come to the conclusion, based simply on <b>
  <i>This Book</i>
</b>, that <b>LIFE IS NOT FAIR!</b> I suppose I should grant <b>
  <i>This Book</i>
</b> some credit for educating me the verities &amp; realities of life.<br /><br />Nope. I guess not. Brooks, you suck for <b>
  <i>This Book</i>
</b>.<br /><br />I wouldn't review <b>
  <i>This Book</i>
</b> after all this time, but it still sticks in my craw (you think?) &amp; recently I read an excellent review by my friend Stephen who pointed out all the problems I remember so well in his fabulous review here:<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/105819358">http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="3803375595524480527" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_282600723" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/282600723" />
    <a title="Stefan Yates" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7590340-stefan-yates"><img alt="Stefan Yates" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1328116275p2/7590340.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/282600723?book_show_action=true">Feb 23, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stefan Yates" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stefan Yates" href="/user/show/7590340-stefan-yates">Stefan Yates</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780394413334" href="/book/show/999140.The_Sword_of_Shannara">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7590340-stefan-yates?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7590340-stefan-yates?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer282600723" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13446073211085816403">This was my second reading of this novel and I think that I may have enjoyed it more the second time around than I did the first. When I read it the first time, I was fairly young and I think that the sheer size of it overwhelmed me a bit. This reading, however, I went in with lowered expectations because of all of the negative vibe that this book has taken and was more than pleasantly surprised to find that I still really enjoy it.<br/><br/>To stop the critics right here: yes, The Sword of Shannara does </span>
  <span id="freeText13446073211085816403" style="display:none">This was my second reading of this novel and I think that I may have enjoyed it more the second time around than I did the first. When I read it the first time, I was fairly young and I think that the sheer size of it overwhelmed me a bit. This reading, however, I went in with lowered expectations because of all of the negative vibe that this book has taken and was more than pleasantly surprised to find that I still really enjoy it.<br /><br />To stop the critics right here: yes, The Sword of Shannara does have some elements that strongly resemble The Lord of the Rings. I will argue, however, that I did not find these resemblances to be nearly as profuse as some would lead you to believe nor did I feel the need to downgrade the author for being influenced by one of the greatest fantasy creations of all time. Homer was inspired by legends and oral tales; Virgil was inspired by Homer; and authors throughout the history of the written word have been inspired by those who came before them. To downgrade Terry Brooks as an author simply because his story bears a passing resemblance at times to something great that came before him is simply unfair.<br /><br />Brooks writes in very nicely flowing, descriptive style. His storyline is fast-paced moving his characters from one adventure to the next in their ongoing journey to complete their overall quest. Some things are a little predictable from time to time, but Brooks does have plenty of surprises and other twists that keep readers on their toes and this large novel actually reads rather quickly. <br /><br />Overall, I enjoyed the novel thoroughly and thumb my nose at all of the hatred that is heaped upon it by those unwilling to give something similar to a great work credit in its own right.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13446073211085816403" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1520652103" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1520652103" />
    <a title="Laura P." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4492808-laura-p"><img alt="Laura P." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1599681786p2/4492808.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1520652103?book_show_action=true">Jan 22, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Laura P." class="user" itemprop="url" name="Laura P." href="/user/show/4492808-laura-p">Laura P.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781841495484" href="/book/show/891775.The_Sword_of_Shannara">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1520652103" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7705885373025085214">Actual rating: 3.60 stars.<br/><br/>This book was a journey. <br/>After spending 14 days reading this before bedtime (1 or 2 chapters/day)...I'm almost teary eyed.<br/><br/>The first 170 pages were slow, the narration dull but the plot interesting..and then it finally picked up.<br/>I liked the journey both physical and personal that Shea undertakes...<br/>I loved Balinor and his Border legion, Eventine and the Elven warriors, and of course Durin & Dayel<br/>I was intrigued by Allanon. And of course I can't not mention Menion (which I</span>
  <span id="freeText7705885373025085214" style="display:none">Actual rating: 3.60 stars.<br /><br />This book was a journey. <br />After spending 14 days reading this before bedtime (1 or 2 chapters/day)...I'm almost teary eyed.<br /><br />The first 170 pages were slow, the narration dull but the plot interesting..and then it finally picked up.<br />I liked the journey both physical and personal that Shea undertakes...<br />I loved Balinor and his Border legion, Eventine and the Elven warriors, and of course Durin &amp; Dayel<br />I was intrigued by Allanon. And of course I can't not mention Menion (which I really liked a lot)and Hendel.<br />Basically I loved the whole company and how their friendship grew and they bonded over adversities.<br />The book was full of action and I loved the battles and cried the dead.<br /><br />Only a couple of things bothered me<br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br />- I was expecting something more "epic" from the sword<br />- I found the declaration of love between Shril and Menion, preoposterous...I would have been okay if they had just stuck together. But seriously they had been knowing each other for two pages and barely spoken at that..bah. It was seriously ridiculous.<br />- Why did we have to kill Handel &amp; Kelset...it was too sad!  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />All in all it was a good book, I'm happy to have read it.<br /><br />By the way I have read a lot of comments about the similarities with LOTR but to me the only thing they have in common is that they follow the "traditional fantasy recipe" and that's it.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780345535139" href="/book/show/13531074-the-sword-of-shannara">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12581658-noel?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1240537394" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17475071677605087735">Something about this book made me feel like a kid again. Like when you're young, and discovering fantasy books, and the magic of them draws you in and you're completely awed and amazed. It's unfortunate that I didn't actually read this when I was younger, because I'm sure I would have liked it even more than I did right now. But even so, I loved it. <br/>And yes, it's similar to LOTR. That really doesn't bother me. I think it's better actually.</span>

          </span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('i4yTQLmHJjz8kwazc2cNMkxCbgkSxuyKuqkeitJYaGMYV0SPTLMTru87Ms1RAXsxzYyNLpmWRXxvQhNdAIX79g==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('hc6SWIcqxXKmCkj7zOSf9/6OYgpIDzdHTz5qFzQLmiEWFUWXch7w4LWifIXugun0f0CBLcNfnrGa1WfA5tYJtA==')})
  }

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/9629.Terry_Brooks">About Terry Brooks</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/9629.Terry_Brooks"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1280785812p3/9629.jpg);'></div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer12978936395604785900">Terry Brooks was born in Illinois in 1944, where he spent a great deal of his childhood and early adulthood dreaming up stories in and around Sinnissippi Park, the very same park that would eventually become the setting for his bestselling Word & Void trilogy. He went to college and received his undergraduate degree from Hamilton College, where he majored in English Literature, and he received his</span>
  <span id="freeText12978936395604785900" style="display:none">Terry Brooks was born in Illinois in 1944, where he spent a great deal of his childhood and early adulthood dreaming up stories in and around Sinnissippi Park, the very same park that would eventually become the setting for his bestselling Word &amp; Void trilogy. He went to college and received his undergraduate degree from Hamilton College, where he majored in English Literature, and he received his graduate degree from the School of Law at Washington &amp; Lee University.<br />A writer since high school, he wrote many stories within the genres of science fiction, western, fiction, and non-fiction, until one semester early in his college years he was given The Lord of the Rings to read. That moment changed Terry's life forever, because in Tolkien's great work he found all the elements needed to fully explore his writing combined in one genre.<br />He then wrote The Sword of Shannara, the seven year grand result retaining sanity while studying at Washington &amp; Lee University and practicing law. It became the first work of fiction ever to appear on the New York Times trade paperback bestseller list, where it remained for over five months.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12978936395604785900" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
